Members ofthe publicmay testifyinthe Council chamber, at courtesytestimony sites,
or remotely through the informationlistedon the meeting agenda. Individualsinthe
Council chamber may sign up to testifywith the stafflocatedatthe desk inthe eighth-
floorlobby.
Individualsat courtesy testimony sitesmay sign up with staffat the site.Individuals
participatingremotely may sign up in the meeting chat. Ifyou are connected to the
meeting by phone, we willbe unmuting you to see when you willbe testifying.
Individualsconnected by phone are currentlyon mute and willbe unmuted when itis
theirtime to testify.Individualsconnected by video conferenceshould keep both their
video and microphones offand should turnthem on onlywhen itistheirtime totestify.
Testimony islimitedto the items listedon the agenda. Individualsmay testifyforthree
minutes with up to one minute to conclude per item. When testifying,please stateyour
name and the name of any organizationyou represent,as wellas the items on which
you'llbe testifying.Please also identifyto the Council ifyou are a paid lobbyist.
Individualsmay also be disconnected from the meeting at any time for breaking
decorum. At thistime,individualsmay testifyon ceremonial resolutions.
Chair, we have one individualcurrentlysigned up to testifyon ceremonial resolutions.

And we need to stand up forone another as we’re healingfrom these traumas, so that

MR. TRACY BENNETT: Happy Aloha Friday. Mahalo, Chair. Mahalo. Member King,and
Members of our Maui County Council. I'm very honored to be recognizedforthis.It
was an incrediblydifficulttime in allof our lives.We were shut down completely.
Resorts were closed, businesses, restaurants. There was no clear end insight.
And so, in the Summer of 2020, Donne Dawson, our State Film Commissioner and i
created thismodified filmand TV quarantine program thatreliedon robusttestingand
isolation.And the factthatthisHBO production was able to buy out the Four Seasons
Resort for three months and shoot a tv series there was one of the firstproductions in
the world to create a COVID-free bubble. With the Four Seasons and our local crew
and cast,once you were in,there was nobody out.
And Donne and 1 had to take this modified film and TV quarantine program to
Mayor Victorinofor approval,and to Governor Ige for approval. And at thatpoint,
Regular Meeting ofthe Council ofthe County of Maui
October 21, 2022
Page 12
Governor Ige deemed the filmand TV industryas essential.And Ithinkanybody with
a TV, anybody who has a subscriptionto Netflix,Hulu, Amazon, cable, Spectrum,
DirectTV, Ithinkthatshows how importantthe industryisincreatingcontent forpeople
to watch.
Going back to the Summer of 2020, itwas a very difficulttime,
coordination between the Four Seasons, between HBO, and our cast and crew here.
And our localcast and crew literallyhad to move intothe Four Seasons for several
months to shoot. And while itsounds likea great vacation,itwasn't. There was no
going to the pool. There was hanging outside. There was no going to restaurants.
And there was no going to the beach. And we arranged with Mayor Victorinoa period
of time of a few days where they were allowed out intothe community, onto the beach,
to Olowalu and to Maalaea Harbor, were the only other three locationsthey shot at
other than the Four Seasons.
It took a lot of
So, itcreated a sense of comfort aftersome obvious community pushback earlierin
the pandemic. And itwas importantforDonne and 1to make sure thatour community
feltsafe,thatwe were protectingthe aina,we were protectingour residents,and we
were protectingour localcrew. And itdeemed very successful.And two weeks into
filmingthe show, 1knew thatitwas going to be good. Iwent back tothe Mayor'sOffice.
I went to Joann Inamasu. I went to Donne Dawson. I toldeverybody thisisgoing to
be a great show. It'sgoing to win awards. And sure enough, itgarnered a record-tying
20 Emmy nominations. And they won ten. they won every category they were
nominated in.
And itwas justa,such a pleasureto see something likethatgrow outofa periodwhere
we had a very tough time. And to get the accolades thatitdidwas amazing. And I'm
justhappy tobe acknowledged forthis.And I'dliketosay thankyou toJoann Inamasu,
your continued support and understanding of the industryand what ittakes to get it
going,and to diversifyour economy here. Ithinkwe've proven thatwe can take steps
inthe rightdirectionto reallymake itgrow.
The motion pictureand televisionindustryisone ofthe biggestindustriesinthe State
of Hawaii and IwillletDonne speak to those numbers injusta second. But it'sthe
biggest industryoutsideof what we had here, sugarcane, and the amount of dollars
thatitbringsin,the amount of people itputs to work. And tobe recognizedforsuch a
greatshow like"The White Lotus",while itisa ratedR show, ittouched on community,
ittouched on staffworkers at the resorts, ittouched on the Hawaiian culture.There's
some beautifulHawaiian music in it.And they make the scenery ofwhat Maui County
was, absolutelygorgeous. Some excellentwriting,directing,acting.

Resolution 22-187 would approve cost items for Police Officersincluded within

for Fiscal Years 2022 to 2025.

practicesforeach purpose.

Discussion? Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernandez.
VICE-CHAIR RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ: Mahalo, Chair. Your Budget, Finance, and Economic
Development Committee met on August 4, and October 5, 2022, to discuss
Bill102 (2022). This billwould amend Sections 3.48.305(B), Maui County Code, to
prohibitpropertieswith transientvacation rentalsfrom receivingthe home exemption.
This billwould close a loophole in the currenttax legislationaffectinga homeowner
who operates a transientvacation rentalon the propertyand who continuesto reside
on the property.This loopholeenables the homeowner to remain classifiedas Owner-
Occupied and qualifyforthe home exemption. Ifthisbillisenactedthepropertywould
be reclassified as Commercial Residential and taxed accordingly.
Your Committee voted 5-0 to recommend passage on first reading of
Bill102, CD1 (2022). I ask forthe Members support of thismotion and willyieldto
Committee Vice-Chair Paltin on her amendment in CC 22-262. Mahalo, Chair.

MS. JORDAN MOCKER (testifyingon Resolution No. 22-241):
Aloha. Chair Lee, Vice-Chair Rawlins-Fernandez, and Councilmembers. Thank you
for having me today. My name isJordan Hocker and I'llbe testifyingon Resolution
22-241, regardingthe County urging Kaiser Permanente to do the rightthing. So, I've
testifiedinfrontofthisbody before. My community advocacy isinhomeless outreach.
And I beg the question to thisbody ifhoused people cannot have access to mental
healthcare due to Kaiser's current policiesand choices, how do you think that our
unsheltered are accessing thatcare?
Back when Kaiser Permanente took over our hospitalsystem, Ibelieve they also took
over responsibilityto serve our community in a way that was righteous. And they're
not doing that.As you heard testifiers,the currentprofessionalswho are on strikeare
not on strikebecause they can affordto do so. They're not on strikebecause they feel
liketaking a day offof work. They're on strikebecause Kaiser Permanente's policies
have leftthem no other choice. Itisthe laststep.
And for a littleframe of reference, Kaiser Permanente has had many strikes. All
throughout California,theirnurses, other healthcare professionalshave had to either
threatento go on striketo the tune of 32,000 employees saying we're going to step out
before anything gets done. Inthe State of California,Legislaturehad to be passed that
made sure that Kaiser Permanente patientswere followed up when they sought care
withina timely manner.
This isa multi-billion-dollarcorporation. There isabsolutelyno reason thatthey cannot
be hiringmore people. UH Maui College has a human servicestrack. They could be
hiringpeople from Maui to serve our community. So, in listeningto these folks,you
heard Marlena. Oh, thank you, Noe, my baby woke up. You hear Marlena. When I
firstjoined them on the picketline,because I'vebeen out there as many weeks as I've
been able to. You know, these are members of our community. And as Italkedto
Marlena, I found out our daughters going to same school. They're both in Kula
Kaiapuni. They're both over in Paia. And it'saffectingher familyto have to step out in

AUTHORIZING PROCEEDINGS IN EMINENT

MAUKA/POHAKEA WATERSHED, MAUI,

1 MOVE TO PASS RESOLUTION 22-206 ON SECOND AND
FINAL READING.

COUNCILMEMBER SiNENCI:
SECOND.
Regular Meeting of the Council ofthe County of Maui
October 21, 2022
Page 123
CHAIR LEE: Seconded by Member Sinenci,moved by Member King, to pass Resolution
22-206 on second and finalreading.
Discussion, Member King.
COUNCILMEMBER KING; Thank you, Chair. Members, Resolution 22-206 passed first
reading on October 2 [sic],with six "ayes",two "noes", and one Member "excused".
This resolutionauthorizes eminent domain proceedings for the acquisitionof real
property comprised of 257 acres, more or less, and identifiedas Tax Map
Key (2)3-6-001:018 in Maalaea, Maui, Hawaii forpreservation.
As we have discussed at both the CARE Committee and Council, this resolution will
provide another toolto the Administrationto use ifitwants to pursue ownership of this
property. As noted by the Committee, the publicinterestto acquire the propertyisfor
watershed projects,open space, reservoirdevelopment, firesuppression, publicparks,
and possible forestrypreserve.
Housing development agreements were tried on this property and have been
subsequently turned down by the South Maui community over and over again,
including the most recent proposal for gentlemen farming estates. The Council
recognized thatthe water tablecould not support both the Waikapu Town Estates and
development inthisMaalaea area. As our Maui Island Plan expert Dick Mayer stated,
thispropertywas never meant to be developed forhousing.
The Pohakea Stormwater Management Plan recognized thisspecificparcelas having
significantpotentialto mitigatesediment transportto the ocean through a number of
restorationactivities.This parcel has been well-recognized as more valuable to public
purpose ifkept in conservation,especiallysince the State DLNR has supported the
County's recent effortsto preserve the land as open space.
The Trust for Public Land has triedto negotiate with the previous owner, and again
with the current owner, with no luck. Itwas not the, that once we approved the Trust
for Public Land funds going, the County funds going to Trust for Public Lands, itwas
not up to the Council to negotiate. This was put in the hands of the Trust forPublic
Lands.
To reiterate,thisresolutionisan authorizationto give the Administrationanother tool
to negotiate the purpose, the purchase of the named property. Itdoes not bind the
Council or the Administration. But having this tool will hopefully expedite the
negotiationfor the property to be finallyplaced in conservation as soon as possible.
Regular Meeting ofthe Council ofthe County of Maui
October 21,2022
Page 124
And you allheard the urgency from our community. Thank you, Members. Iask for
your continued support ofthisresolution.

Iam a registeredlobbyist.
Bill159 was initiallyreferredby the Council to the Maui County Planning Commission.
The proposed measure was sent to the Paia-Haiku, South Maui, and the Hana
Advisory Committees forinput.The Planning Commission initiallyheard the resolution
and received testimony:however, due to the procedural errorwe justheard about,the
measure was postponed so thatthe requiredrecommendation could be received.
The Planning Commission has received significantcommunity input and stillhas
testimony open forBill159. Accordingly,the Planning Commission has not provided
Regular Meeting of the Council of the County of Maui
October 21, 2022
Page 142
a recommendation, which would include the comments of the Advisory Committees
and community members.
ARDA Hawaii stronglyopposes Bill159 as currentlydrafted.The measure willrepeal
the temporary moratorium on new transientaccommodations and instead make the
moratorium permanent. The originalmoratorium was justestablishedinJanuary. This
moratorium isalready ineffectand should be reviewed foritsoveralleffectivenessin
tourism management before another moratorium overrides and makes itpermanent.
The current two-year moratorium should be utilizedto gather data to determine
whether stopping the development oftransientaccommodations willactuallydecrease
the number of visitors.Further, ARDA Hawaii maintains itspositionthatthe proposed
billwillnot accomplish the overalldesired effect,limitingarrivalsto Maui.
From an economic standpoint,and you've heard a lotofthisbeforeformonths, ARDA
Hawaii is concerned thiscap willlimitjob growth in Maui. Reducing job growth will
reduce tax revenue growth forMaui and also reduce opportunitiesforMaui residents
to findgood localjobs. Timeshare resortscontributesignificanttaxes inrealproperty
tax, GET, TAT, and provides substantial charitable giving to the community.
Specifically,as you allknow, timeshares pay the highest rateof realpropertytax.
Finally,a unilateralcap on timeshare resorts,could resultinthe flourishingof illegal
transient rentals which evade taxes, do not contribute to job growth, and negatively
impact the qualityof life.
Ultimately,the proposed legislationwill unnecessarily establish a permanent
moratorium. While ARDA Hawaii acknowledges the growth. I’llwrap up, ifImay? That
growth to the tourism industryof Maui should not be infiniteand should be sustainably
managed, preventing any form of growth fortourism industrywillresultin unintended
negative consequences. Growth should be reasonable and properlymanaged rather
than precluded.
ARDA Hawaii isinfavor of working with allCouncilmembers and stakeholders. We're
very encouraged to hear therewas compromises discussed. But as withthe Chamber,
we haven't seen those in writingyet and would likethe opportunityto comment on
those as well. Thank you very much.

Honorable Members of the Maui County Council:
I’m writing again to urge you to vote against the passage of Resolution No. 22-206. At the
October 7^ council meeting, I discussed our commitment to doing the right thing for the
community and our process of deciding what could be done on the site. Today, I’dlike to
provide an update on our community outreach effortsand development of stormwater
solutions:
We’ve met with community stakeholders, including those who had favored eminent
domain. We shared productive conversations about open space, fireprevention, long
term stormwater solutions and the potential for a workforce housing community for
local families. I’m deeply grateful to those who’ve engaged in dialogue, even under
the shadow of eminent domain; it’sa great collaborative starting point.
We’re coordinating with a prominent environmental leader to co-host a volunteer
community cleanup in November.
We’ve met with State of Hawaii program managers regarding potential energy storage
projects and developing a climate change resilience hub.
West Maui Construction’s survey team is mapping out our property and portions of
the surrounding State land. A detailed topographic map willbe generated to form the
basis for designing successful stormwater improvements.
We’ve performed a preliminary assessment of existing drainage infrastructure in the
region to understand where improvements are needed most. Documentation is
attached.
We’ve received expert recommendations for interim solutions to reduce erosion and
runoff while we go through the eminent domain process, or preferably, the workforce
housing approval process.
We’ve implemented repairs to the existing wells and piping, making the property’s
water system now fullyoperational, and ready to support agricultural activitiesand
new plantings for erosion control.
We’d also like to work together with you to improve the existing County-owned basin
behind the Ma’alaea condos. This is listedas a “high priorityrecommendation” in Section
1
4.3.4 of the Pohakea Watershed/Ma'alaea Bay Stormwater Management Plan prepared by
Maui Environmental Consulting.
West Maui Construction and Hope Builders are committed to improving this land and its
water system regardless of how the Council votes on eminent domain. WeVe not just
landowners, we’re also community members who care deeply about improving this
beautiful island we call home. Our goal for this property is to improve it,not to own it
forever. We want to pass on responsibility to hundreds of local familieswho willdo a better
job of tending the land. Ifthe County takes itsooner, that just means well have less time
to make improvements, but well stilltry to do good work in the meantime.
Upon the completion of our topographic survey, we’d liketo have community meetings to
explore and collaborate on stormwater solutions, firerisk mitigation, open space concepts,
and creating a climate change resiliencehub. This community engagement willbe the
foundation for creating a workforce housing community for generations to come.
This is a long process, and we need more time. Please don’t say “No” at this point. All
we’re asking for is the opportunity to meet the needs of our community. Let’skeep the
dialogue going, and keep working on solutions.
At the end of the day, I think this whole issue reallycomes down to a simple question. Who
will do the best job of caring for this land? A real estate developer? Government
politicians? Or hundreds of individualhomeowners? I put my trustin localpeople to do
the rightthing. Please help Maui’s hardworking families,and vote against eminent domain.
Thank you,
Ryan Grether
2
West Maui Construction, inc.
35 Lunalilo Street,Suite 400
Wailuku, HI 96793

IaIMC
CONTRACTOR: ABC-30250
Preliminary Drainage Assessment
Stormwater flows across 257-acre property at Maalaea,
TMK (2) 3-6-001:018, and stormwater flows across adjacent properties
which enter Maalaea Bay.
Prepared by:
Ryan Grether, lie.#CT-37476
West Maui Construction, Inc.
Mark Matsuda, P.E.
Hope Builders, Inc.
September 27, 2022
Background:
The 257-acre parcel in Maalaea was recently purchased by West Maui
Construction and Hope Builders. This assessment of existing drainage
conditions is based upon detailed fieldinspections to develop a plan to capture
stormwater flows and prevent sediment transport into Maalaea Bay.
InitialFindings:
There is significantpotential for transport of sediment and other pollutants
into Maalaea Bay by stormwater flows across the 257-acre property and the
State-owned land adjacent to that property.
Attached to this report are fivediagrams that show the approximate locations
of significantstormwater flows in and around the 257-acre parcel. These
diagrams were created using images from Google Earth for simplicity,and
because the new property owners have not yet had the opportunity to complete
a formal survey. There are also numerous photos of existing drainage
infrastructure.
Diagram 1 shows an overview of the property and surrounding area. The 257-
acre parcel is represented by the regions highlighted in blue and orange.
● The blue region represents approximately 80% of the total area of the
property. Stormwater flows, originating from the uphill State-owned
lands, transit the blue region of the property and are captured by various
existing drainage culverts. These flow under the highway and into a
County-owned retention basin.
● The orange region represents approximately 20% of the total area of the
property. Stormwater flows, originating from the uphill State-owned
lands, transit the orange region and mix with other stormwater flows
from State lands carrying sediment into Maalaea Harbor. The orange
region has significantpotential for stormwater pollution improvements;
however, this region alone is not enough to resolve the entire area’s
stormwater issues.
Diagram 2 shows the State land to the south of the 257-acre parcel where
stormwater runoff enters Maalaea Harbor. Runoff, which transits the orange
shaded region of the 257-acre property, flows into existing drainage structures
on State land. It then mixes with other runoff from State lands (independent of
the 257-acre parcel).The combined flows then exit into Maalaea Harbor.
Improvements must be made to this region of State land, in addition to the
southern portion of the 257-acre property, in order to implement a
comprehensive solution to the issue of stormwater pollution.
Diagram 3 shows stormwater flows across land further south of the 257-acre
parcel that is owned by the State. These flows can carry sediment and other
pollutants into Maalaea Bay, just outside of Maalaea Harbor. Currently, there
are no stormwater mitigation structures for these flows.
Diagram 4 shows an existing basin owned by the County. This basin collects
flow from:
● Uphill State-owned land;
● Approximately 80% of the area of the 257-acre parcel;
● A portion of runoff from the highway;
This County-owned basin was a “failure”according to the Stormwater
Management Plan dated 11/16/2018 and prepared by Maui Environmental
Consulting. ''Based on the observed failure,itis assumed the basin’s size and
construction are inadequate to handle the substantial flows itreceives.”
Diagram 5 shows the location of photos taken onsite. These photos document
the existing drainage infrastructure, erosion, and discharge locations.
The photos provide two primary observations:
● The erosion of soilon the 257-acre property represents a significant
problem requiring urgent action.
● There are numerous drain inlets in the Maalaea area that allow
pollutants and runoff from roadways to flow directly into the ocean,
o Only the Maui Ocean Center property has subsurface drains to retain
runoff. This is shown on Record Drawings produced by Warren S.
Unemori Engineering, Inc. on 12/11/1997.
Solutions:
Inaction willallow the problem of stormwater runoff into Maalaea Harbor to
worsen. The owners of the 257-acre parcel, working with State and County
officials,can implement a long-term stormwater solution together.
Currently, West Maui Construction’s survey team is mapping out the existing
topography of the land for the purpose of designing stormwater catchment
structures. Additionally, West Maui Construction secured permission from the
State to enter their adjacent land to create a complete survey of the area and
design a long-term solution. All data collected willbe shared.
Recommendations:
1. We recommend two options to remedy the problem of stormwater runoff in
and around the southern portion of the 257-acre property,
a. Construct retention basins with sufficient capacity to capture runoff
generated during large storms,
b. Capture the stormwater flows and distribute itlaterallyacross the
existingterrainusing a system of berms and swales to form contoured
vegetative barriers. Additionally, native plants can be utilizedwithin
these vegetative barriers to retain the topsoil and allow the stormwater to
feed reforestationprojects and/or permaculture farming.
2. To remedy the problem of stormwater runoff across the northern portion of
the 257-acre property, we offersimilar recommendations,
a. Repair and expand the existing County basin to adequately capture
runoff from large storm events.
b. Ifimprovements are not made to the County’s basin, then additional
basins and/or contoured vegetative barriers would need to be
constructed on the northern portion of the 257-acre parcel to limit the
volume of stormwater flow reaching the County’s basin.
3. To prevent pollutants outside of the 257-acre property from entering the
drainage system and flowing into the ocean, we recommend installing drain
inlet filterswithin existing catch basins along roadways. These filtersare
commercially available and easy to installbut will require maintenance
expenditures on the part of the State, County, and/or private landowners.
Currently, West Maui Construction and Hope Builders are in the process of
developing multiple design proposals for systems of basins and/or contoured
vegetative barriers that would span both the 257-acre parcel and State land.
Final design proposals are pending the completion of the topographic survey.
West Maui Construction and Hope Builders will continue to explore stormwater
solutions that address the onsite erosion and continued conveyance of
sediment towards the ocean. Together, ifwe respond thoughtfully and
collaboratively,we can successfully restore the natural ecological integrityof
the land.
Sincerely,
Ryan Grether
Vice President
West Maui Construction, Inc.

TO: Councilmember Alice Lee, Chair
Councilmembcr Keani Rawlins-Femandez, Vice- Chair
Members of theMaui County Council
FR: AMERICAN RESORT DEVELOPMENT ASSOCIATION - HAWAII (ARDA-Hawaii)
RE: Bill 159 - A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COMPREHENSIVE
ZONING ORDINANCE RELATING TO TRANSIENT ACCOMMODATION CAPS
Hearing date: Friday, October 21, 2022 at 9:00AM
Aloha Chair Lee Vice Chair Rawlins-Femandez and members of the Maui County Council,
Thank you forallowingARDA-Hawaii to submit testimonyprovidingOPPOSITION to Bill
159 - A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COMPREHENSIVE ZONING
ORDINANCE RELATING TO TRANSIENT ACCOMMODATION CAPS. Bill 159 seeks to
amend Title19 of theMaui County Code (MCC) to establishtransientaccommodations caps.
ARDA Hawaii strongly opposes Resolution 22-70 as currently drafted. The measure will
repeal the temporary moratorium on new transientaccommodations and insteadmake the
moratorium permanent. The originalmoratorium (Ordinance5316) was justestablishedinJanuary
of this year. This moratorium is already in effectand should be reviewed for itsoverall
effectivenessin tourism management before another moratorium overridesand makes it
permanent. The currenttwo-year moratorium should be utilizedto gather data to determine
whether stoppingthe development of transientaccommodations will decreasethe number of
visitorsto Maui. Further,ARDA Hawaii maintainsitspositionthatthe proposed billwillnot
accomplish theoveralldesiredeffectof limitingarrivalsto the Maui.
From an economic standpoint,ARDA-Hawaii isconcerned thatthiscap willlimitjob growth
in Maui. Reducing jobs growth will reduce tax revenue growth for Maui and also reduce
opportunitiesforMaui residentsto find localgood paying jobs.For example, the average pay for
timesharesalesand marketing positionson Maui was 130K annually(2016 data)and theaverage
pay fortimeshareresortoperationspositionson Maui was 63,000K (2016 data).Timeshare resorts
s contributesignificanttaxesin RPT, GET, TAT and providesubstantialcharitablegivingtothe
community. Specifically,timesharespay the highestrateof RPT at $14.60 per $1,000 of net
taxableassessedvaluation.Finally,a unilateralcap on timeshareresorts,could resultin the
flourishingof illegaltransientrentalswhich evade taxes,do not contributeto job growth,and
negativelyimpact the qualityof lifeinMaui’s residentialneighborhoods.
1
Ultimately,the proposed legislationwillunnecessarilyestablisha permanent moratorium on
transientaccommodations. While ARDA-Hawaii acknowledges that growth of the tourism
industryon Maui should not be infiniteand should be sustainablymanaged, preventingany form
of growth for the tourism industrywillresultin unintended negativeeconomic consequences.
Growth inan industryshouldbe reasonableand properlymanaged ratherthan precludedentirely.
ARDA Hawaii isin favorof working with allcouncilmembers and stakeholdersto cooperate
on legislationthatproperlymanages tourismon Maui. We welcome any opportunitytocollaborate
with all stakeholders on any amendments including those considered in the Planning and
SustainableLand Use Committee. The timeshare industryunderstands the concerns voiced by
residentsand looks forwardto supportingand contributingto Maui County.
Thank you foryour considerationof my comments.
Respectfullysubmitted,
Mitchell A. Imanaka
ARDA Hawaii Chair

COUNTY CLERKDear Maui County Councilmembers,
On behalf of Maui PRMA, the Vacation Rental Trade Council under the Maui Chamber of Commerce,
we ask that Bill 159 return back to committee to allow the Planning Commission to complete
their review.
PRMA, the Professional Rental Management Association, is a coalitionof professionalproperty
management companies representing over 1600 legallyzoned condominium vacation rental
units throughout Maui. Our members are licensed in the State of Hawaii, engaged in the
management of legalvacation rental properties,primarily condominiums, and comply with real
estate licenselaw and code of ethics.Our companies represent 216 years in business,employing
nearly 200 employees and over 300 independent contractorsand vendors.
Our industryishighlyimpacted by Bill159 and yet,we have not yet been calledas a resource
group, invitedto the tableor given the chance to share our concerns and input.
This billshould continue to be vetted in committee and allow the commission to complete their
review. More voices need to be heard as we do not feel this billhas been a collaborative effort. The
planning commission should be allowed to give theirrecommendation and they have not been
allowed to do their work.
It'sour hope thatwe can finda balance and way as a county tocreatethe affordablehousing
needed and manage tourism without the need totakeaway and negativelyimpactour locally
owned and run small businesses.
On behalfof PRMA, we ask thatyou would NOT PASS Bill159 but allow itto return to committee
for further review.
Thank you foryour considerationand we welcome any discussionwith you or a member ofyour
administration and we can be contacted at Mauiprma@gmail.com.
Mahalo,
John Kevan
Angela Leone
Maui ProfessionalRental Management Association(Maui PRMA)

the islands.As long as visitorsarrive,they willfind a place to stay.In introducinga cap, other

tents on the rise.They are growing because we do not have effectivelaws and enforcement in placeto
controlthem, and they are not limitedto where they can be in our community. Our hotel and
timeshare propertiesare alreadybeholden to strictdevelopment and zoning laws.

and realproperty tax billswillhave the potentialfor massive appeals due to the decrease in property
values. Where will the RPT revenues come from to make up for thisloss in revenue?

Aloha and good Morning Council members,
1am writinginsupport of the followingItems on today'sagenda:
1. Bill154 (2022) relatingto the development of Culturaloverlaydistricts

PAIAINN
93 Hana Hwy

Z022OCT I9 PH 25
OFFICE OF THE
The Paia Inn buildinghas been a historicalmainstay inthetownofPaiaforhebriyflW^^fsPih^
2001, we purchased the buildingwhich was builtback in 1927 as a traditionalJapanese Inn,
and at the County’s advice, began a restorationand preservation projectso thatthe building
could continue to be utilizedas itwas originallyintended while preserving itshistoriccharm. In
2008, we were able to re-open what was once known as the Paia Lodge, as the Paia Inn and it
has since been consistentlyrecognized as one of Maui’stop hospitalityaccommodations on the
island.
Throughout itsoperation,the Paia Inn has provided tremendous value to the greater community
as a whole. Guests frequentthe many localbusinesses throughout Paia Town, spending their
money in Paia’s shops and restaurantshelping to support the localeconomy. Additionally,we
employ many Maui County residentswho also end up contributingto our localeconomy and the
Paia Inn activelymakes charitablecontributionsto schools and nonprofitsislandwide. The Paia
Inn providestremendous value to not only Paia Town, but Maui County as a whole.
Not too long ago, the County recognized thisvalue. Back in2012, the Maui Island Plan was
adopted inorder to provide directionforfuturegrowth, the economy, and socialand
environmental decisions on the islandthrough 2030. One ofthe policiesthe Maui IslandPlan
callsforin managing the futureexpansion of the visitorindustryisspecificallyallowing for the
development of small, sensitively-designed inns. In2014, just8 years ago, the Maui County
Council,while looking at how to carry out the policygoals laidout inthe Maui IslandPlan,
unanimously voted 8-0 to enact Ordinance 4153. Among other things.Ordinance 4153
amended Maui County Code § 19.15.030 to allowforthe operation of up to 12 TVR rooms as a
special use inthe BCT district.The Paia Inn only has 9 rooms.
After the Council enacted Ordinance 4153, we applied to convert 4 officespaces intoTVR
rooms. The plan did not involveany new constructionor development, yet,itwas initially
denied. Aftera long contentious appeal, however, we were able to receive a renewable County
Special Use Permit (CUP) to operate the Paia Inn as a 9 room TVR operationfor10 years.
Retired Judge McConnell, who served as the Hearing Officer,specificallyconcluded that our
familyrun operationwould not have any significantnegative impacts on the community. In fact,
Judge McConnell’s decision specificallynoted thatthere were numerous lettersof support from
adjacent neighbors. Paia community leaders,and fellowbusiness owners.
At the March 17, 2022 meeting before thisvery Committee, there was some discussion
suggesting thatthe billas itiscurrentlydraftedwould not affectthe Paia Inn,and Ms. McLean
specificallystated thatwe “should be able to renew.” To Corp Counsel’s credit,Mr. Hopper
chimed in and explained, however, thatthiswas not true. He specificallystatedthatunder the
current language of the bill,we would not be able to renew our Permit and itwould ultimately
expire. Then, at the August 9, 2022 Maui Planning Commission meeting, the Planning
Bill159 (2022)
Testimony in Opposition
Department testifiedsuggesting thatthisbillisnot intended to affectany existingTVR
operations and isonly intended to stop any futureoperations from springing up. Clearly,
however, thisis not true. While yes, the Paia Inn willbe able to continue to operate as a
nonconforming use, thiswould only be forthe remainder of the lifeof our CUP and then we
would be precluded from seeking a renewal of the permitjust as Mr. Hopper pointed out back in
March. Our CUP term isup for renewal in 2028.
Further,Councilmember Rawlins-Fernandez has “acknowledged includingthe provisionthat
could kill[thePaia Inn]afterhearing concerns and reading testimony from some of [the]
neighbors, including[Ms.]Aarona.” In fairness,however, itmust also be mentioned thatwhen
Judge McConnel issued his Decision essentiallyorderingthe County to grant our CUP, he
specificallypointed out thatMs. Aarona’s testimony was "irrelevantand should be disregarded
as he found that itwas “notsupported by the evidence” and affectedby her “personal issues
with Mr. Baskin.”
To the best of our knowledge, the Paia Inn isthe only entitywho has been granted a CUP to
operate TVR rooms inthe BCT thatwillbe directlyimpacted by Section 4 of the proposed bill
which willremove TVR as a special use in the BCT district.We did findanother entitywho
received a CUP to operate TVR rooms inthe BCT districton Molokai, however, to our
understanding the new buildingthey were seeking to buildhas yet to be constructed. We,
however, are up and running,employing localresidentsand providing a boost to the economy of
Paia Town, allthe while not having any negative impact on the surrounding properties,owners,
or the County.
This Billisextremely unfairand unjustas itpertainsto the Paia Inn. We, and our staff,should
not have to sufferthe consequence of being forced out of business once our permit expires. We
are a familyrun business operating a small sensitivelydesigned inn providing nothing but a
benefitto the community. Infiveyears, itwillbe a hundred years since the constructionof the
Paia Inn Building. Itisa historicstaple located rightinthe heart of Paia and should be
celebrated.
We stronglyurge you to oppose the billoutright,however, ifyou are not inclinedto do so, we
would propose an amendment thatwould either:(1)deletethe portionof the billthatwould
remove TVR as a specialuse inthe BCT district;or (2) includea provisionthatwould
specificallyallow currentpermit holders to continue to operate indefinitelyso long as they are in
compliance with the conditionsof theirpermit. We also urge you to consider carving out an
exception that would allow current property owners, who submit an applicationfor a CUP to
operate TVR rooms as a special use in the BCT districtwithin 180 days from the effectivedate
of the bill,to continue operating indefinitelyas a nonconforming use. Thank you foryour time
and consideration on thisextremely important measure.
Mahalo.
Michael Baskin
Paia inn

PleaseDO NOT cap vacationrentals
To:
Subject:
[You don'toften get email from steve@sacampbell.com. Learn why thisisimportant at
https://aka.ms/LearnAboutSenderldentification]
Dear Maul County Council Members,
As a 24 year Wailea Maui property owner Iwish to express my oppositionto effortsto a curb or inany way, limitshort
term vacation rentalson the part of condominium owners or theiragents. The reasonsthatI,and many property
owners objectto such effortsare as follows:
1).Limitingor inanyway capping condo vacationrentalsinareaswhere condosarevaluedinexcessof$1.5M willdo
nothing to solvethe affordablehousing crisis.Why? The carrycost{taxes,fees,overhead,debt coverage)ofthese
properties,most often in Makena and Wailea area,are farinexcess of what would representa monthly fairmarket
rental. In fact,in these ocean front zones, median propertyvaluesare approaching$3.5M. Faced with rentallimitsof
any kind,property values would decline,mortgage lenders would likelyreduce loanto value lendingcriteria,and county
property tax and rentaltax revenues would declinesignificantly.The onlybeneficiariesof such a policywould be the
largehotels.
2).Far from addressingthe affordablehousing crisis,the proposed measure would createa new crisisintheform of
residentialloan defaults,a likely20-35% declineinocean frontzone condo values,and largescalelayoffsof localpeople
employed to maintain,clean,repair,and manage these shortterm rentalcondos. Similarly,the smallbusinessesand
trades that provide servicesto condo owners (carpetcleaners,window washers,repairtechs,and plumbers/electricians
willsuffer,as willthe numerous restaurants and shops who willsee a declineinbusinessas fewer guestswillbe ableto
find accommodation.
3).Maui's affordablehousing crisisisa complex problem. Workable solutionsmust notcreatemassiveunintended
consequences such as thisproposal willcause.
Thank you foryour considerationof these objections,and Iurgeyou tovote againsttheseefforts.
Respectfully,
Stephen Campbell
3300 Wailea Alanui
Wailea Kihei Maui

Dear Chair Lee and Members of Maui County Council,
On behalf of Expedia Group, a family of brands that includes Expedia.com,
Hotels.com, and short-term rental leader Vrbo, Iam writingto share testimony on Bill
159,a billamending the comprehensive zoning ordinance relatingto transient
accommodation caps.
We know that Maui County isengaged ina deep and criticalconversation about the
impacts and future of itstourism sector. Expedia Group firmlysupports effortsto
responsiblymanage tourism and has worked with municipalitiesaround the world to
craft,enact, and support regulations and legislationto stabilizethe tourism ecosystem.
While we may support balanced accommodations policy,there are a number of
concerns and questions about Bill159,a sweeping policythat must be considered
carefullywith significantpublic input.
Given the number of changes that were discussed at yesterday’sPlanning and
Sustainable Land Use Committee meeting, we respectfullyurge Council to provide
additional time to review updated legislationand weigh inon the amended text.For
example, depending on the finallanguage, changes to Section 20 could radicallyalter
the legislationand jeopardize residents’vested rightsto continue to use propertiesas
transient vacation rentals.
Additional time would allow the community and Council to evaluate the long-term
effectsof proposed zoning changes and to better understand any legalor financial
consequences.
We are committed to being a partner and are eager to engage withany member of
Council on thislegislationand other traveland tourism topics.Thank you forthe
opportunityto share testimony on Bill159 and forconsideringour comments.
Thank you,
Mackenzie Chase
Government AffairsManager, Hawaii

In Favor of the Visitor Accommodation Moratorium
To:

Aloha Members of Maui County Council
Please,help us save thisonce idyllicislandby approving Bill159, the VisitorAccommodation Moratorium.

Dear Maui County Council (the“Council”):
1 am writinginstrongoppositionto Bill159 (the“Bill”)and itsamendment of 19.32.040,
SubsectionI,of the Maui County Ordinances. We area localfamilythathas owned a unitinPuamana
forover fortyyears.The 4th generationisnow growing up and abletotakepartinthiswonderful
community. The abilityto renttheunitas a vacationrentalfrom time totime iscriticalto keepingthe
propertyinthefamily.Withoutthisincome,we would likelybe forcedtoselltheproperty,asthe
propertytaxesand feesaresimplytoo much withouttheadditionalincome.
Section19.32.040was recommended by theMaui County PlanningCommittee in2012 and Maui
County Council unanimously approved itin2013. In2016,section19.32.040was amended toinclude
anotherPUD calledAlealoa,nearNapili,which has a similarlow-densityconditionasPuamana.Both of
thesesitesare desirablerentalpropertiesand have propertytaxratesthatreflecttheadded value.
Removing thislanguagewillresultinfamilieslikeourssellingtheirpropertytosomeonewho canafford
not to rentitout (i.e.,anotherwinterretreatfora non-resident).Thiswillalsoresultinthelossof income
tothepropertymanagers,handymen,cleaners,and many otherlocalbusinessesthatrelyon these
propertiesto make a livinghereon theisland.
Accordingly,we humbly requestthattheCouncileitherreturnBill159tothecommitteefor
furtherrevieworremove theproposedchangestoSection19.32.0401forplanneddevelopments.This
languagewas carefullycreatedand vettedin2013 and shouldnotbe removed,especiallywithouta
thoroughreviewof itseffectsand a greaterdiscussionwiththeaffectedpropertyowners.

respectto theirmental healthworkers. This shows a terribledisregardand value forthe fieldof
mental health.

with theirmental healthworkers? They have been on strikeover two months now, with no
resolution.

patients,likeme, pay our premiums and deservetohave healthcareavailable.In contrast,Kaiser
isjustmaking more money by providinglessservicesas long as they letthisstrikecontinue.

as careforthe body. The pandemic has increasedour collectiveanxietyand many have losta

A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE
ORDINANCE RELATING TO TRANSIENT ACCOMMODATION CAPSRE: Bill 159 (in
supportof) CFFICE OF THE
i:OUNTY CLERK
Aloha Maui County Council Members:
I am writingthisletterinsupportof amending thezoning relatingtotransientaccommodation on
Maui. This cap isa crucialsteptoward remediatingthecurrentunregulatedover-tourismwe are
seeinghere.Prohibitingtheuse of camper vans forvacationrentalsisan extremelyimportant
partof thisBill.Touristswho rentcamper vans areusing up our very limitedresourcesand are
not contributingtothe community atall.
The Maui IslandPlan suggestslimitingthenumber ofvisitorstoapproximately1/3thenumber
of residentsinordertopreserveour environment,infrastructure,and qualityof lifeforresidents—
allof which would improve thevisitorexperienceas well.
The year 2019 was alreadya year of uncontrolledgrowth,fueledby thetourism industry.
Promises were made by leadersduringtheearlypartof thepandemic to improve on thetourism
experience forboth visitorsand residents.Residentswere promised thatthe goalwould be to
decreasethe number of touristswhile protectingtheislands.Since October of 2020, those
promiseshave been completelyforgottenby our leaders,who proudlyannounce thatthegoalof
reaching2019 numbers has been met and now exceeded.
The currentvolume of touristswe were seeingpre-pandemic and now, in2021, duringthe
pandemic,isa threattothehealth,safetyand qualityof lifeof the residentsof Maui, our
environment and wildlife.
Our islandresourcesare very limited.Our inadequatesewage treatment,water,and landfillsare
not meant for this level of use. We are in a severe water shortage,yetonlyresidentsareaffected,
not tourists.While my family’syard driedup and dieddue to not wateringit,the hotelsare
literallysuckingup wateras ifthereisno restriction.While sewage isdischargedintoour
oceans,touristsareovercrowding our beaches and cruellyabusing our wildlife.Our fishing
industryisendangered by the abuse theocean environment isexperiencing.
On Maui, touristsdo notslayinthetouristareas,but driveallovertheisland,causinghuge
trafficcongestion.Touristsdon’t even thinktwice about usingup resourcesmeant forresidents.
I have seen horrificpicturesof the road to Hana being blocked by touristswho choose to park on
the road,blockingtraffic,because of lackof parking.
Residentsareliterallybeing toldthatwe do not count and thatthetourismindustryisall-
powerful. Our mayor has not showed any supportof controllingtourism,includingvetoingthe
lastproposed moratorium forsouthand west Maui and vetoingtheaffordablehousing bill.He
goes out of hisway topleasethebig money brought inby thetourismindustryand mainland
investors. He has made itclear that residents are second class citizens to tourists. It is the
responsibilityof government officialsto ensurethatthereisadequateaffordablehousingfor
thosewho areessentialtomaking our community work (healthcareprofessionals,teachers,
police,socialworkers,restaurantworkers,grocery/retailworkers and yes,workers intourism),
not to incentivizenonresidents’profitingofftourism.
Residentshere sacrificea greatdeal financiallyto livehere and deserve to be able to enjoy the
beaches,hikesand parks. Instead,thereisno room forresidentson any of these.The majority
of residentshere do not depend atallon thetouristindustry—yet allof us aremade to sacrifice
for it.For me, itisabout more than a financialsacrifice,as thisisnot only my birthplacebut
alsothatof my ancestors.Hardworking residentsaretryingnot to chased out by greedy leaders
who putshort-termprofitfirst.
Our economy needs to be diversified.Our childrenneed to be taughtskillsthatwillhelpthem to
succeed in society,ratherthanjustto servetourists.We need a moratorium on futurevisitor
accommodations while solutionscan be implemented,includingleadershipthatsupportsresident
livesover thetourism industry.
I appreciatethe members of theMaui County Council greatly.With few exceptions,you arethe
leaderswho put residentsand the ‘ainafirst.
Mahalo piha,
Kai Duponte
Kai Duponte, MSW

IJust want to say that Icould not possiblysupport a measure to cap accommodations more than Ido rightnow! Itislong
overdue.
There's a millionreasons to cap the hotelsat where they are now and letthem proceed no further,most of which you
likelyhave received many fold.One thing that should be said,thatshould convinceeven the cynicswho placethe profit
margin over the prosperityof the people, isthat thisisa partialfixforan under-discussedsupply-and-demand issue
Maui ishaving with tourists.
Untilmore recently,and as would intuitivelymake sense,as the number of touristsperyear grew, the amount of money
being spent on islandincreased (the question of how much stayson islandand what the trade offisworth isa separate
conversation).However as of at leasta few years before the pandemic, Maui began seeinga plateauof the amount of
money coming ineven though the number of visitorswas increasing.Thisisbecause each visitorisnow spending less
money when they visit.Part of thisisthat the expansion of the airportmade directflightsfrom more locationscheaper,
bringingin more people with lower budgets and lessmoney to giveto localbusinesses.Capping the hotelsat least
begins to slow the runaway train.Finiteaccommodations means hotelpriceswilllikelyrise,meaning thatthe people
who can affordthe hotelsare more likelyto drop money locally,as opposed to onlyshopping at Costco.IloveCostco
don't hear me wrong, it'sa good employer and itpays welland everybody who liveshere desperatelyneeds those
deals.But money spent there doesn't stay here asidefrom the paychecks foremployees.
Iwould hope we can findother creativeways to reduce supplysomewhat even ifthe airporthatesit.ifthislogicisn't
very intuitiveremember that diamonds are actuallyrathercommon, it'sthatallthe diamonds are owned by one
company (De Beers) and they only give out a littleat a time so pricesareastronomical.It'svery importantto obviously
not do anything to furtherpriceout localsby targetingresourceslocalsneed, but Itrustthiscouncil(my favorite
council!)in itsjudgment. Iwish you could justput plentytaxon everythingunlessyou show Hawai'iIDbut Idon'tknow
ifyouguyscando thatornotI®
And allof thisisbefore we talkabout the thingsthat hurtus immediatelyinways thateveryone knows. Dailylife
becoming more and more tourist-first,erosion of naturalspaces from foottraffic,and alsojustplainold regulartraffic
traffic.Long way from two stoplightsinthe 70'syeah?
Anyways plenty people tellingyou allthat stuffand more so Ino need, Ijustadded what Ithought might not be said
enough.
Staystrongyouguys,you proofvotingworks!^

I appreciate the council’seffortbut I strongly oppose this bill.While certain efforts to
manage over tourism should be looked into, this billcould greatly impact our economy
which is heavily dependent on tourism; especiallyas our economy is likelyheading for a
pretty significantrecession. Right now, I am able to provide a good livingfor my family
by servicing vacation rentals.The authors of this billare trying to solve an extremely
complicated issue, by casting a wide net which could end up creating even worse issues
allwithout guaranteeing any of the actual goals willbe met. After reading through this
billthe only thing that looks to be guaranteed isnegative economic impacts on local
service providers, the workforce, and significanttax revenues. Crushing property values
in touristzones won’t keep mainland buyers from scooping up the inventory in those
areas. They willjust buy the condos at a lower price and stay in them a few times a
year. As a result,they won't need housekeepers, handyman, carpet cleaners, window
cleaners, localproperty managers, etc. Again, I think more weight needs to be
placed on the economic impacts of this decision. Maui has always been a hard place to
make a living,please don't make itany harder for us ifyou cannot guarantee the end-
goal. Sometimes it’sbetter to wait on the right decision, then to make things worse. -
Kawika Englert

Dear Maui County Council:
My husband and Iare home owners in Puamana and stronglyoppose thisbill.We are asking that the billbe returned to
the committee to allowthe PlanningCommission to complete theirreview. We requestthatthe PlanningCommittee
recommend the removal of the proposed changes to section19.32.040 Iforplanned developments to the Maui County
Council. This sectionof the county code appliesonly to unitsin Puamana, Kaanapali Plantationand Alaeloa that were
builtand used forTransientVacation rentalpriorto April20,1989. This part of the county code was establishedin 2013
to clarifythe long standing legalTVR uses inthese specificprojectsand helps the planning department when approving
buildingpermits and SMA exemptions forremodels and renovationsof these older units.Itwas created specificallyto
prevent there ever being any question about the rightfor unitsinthese communities to be used forshortterm
rentals. Itdoes NOT allow new visitor accommodations to be builtor converted from residentialto TVR use; they have
been used forthispurpose sincetheirdevelopment inthe latesixties/seventies.The proposed deletionof thispartof
the existingcode turnsthe legalTVR use intoan “existingnon conforming” use and makes any renovationsor remodels
difficultto get permit approvals.The PlanningCommission should be allowed to do theirwork and providetheir
recommendation.
Mahalo foryour consideration.
Anne and Christopher Fender
87-1 Pualei Drive
Lahaina, HI 96761

October 21, 2022 Maui Council Meeting: Bill159

Maui Council Meeting October 21, 2022 - Bill159:
Council Members,
We have been ov\/ners in Puamana since 2011 and members of our familyhave owned and/or rented inthis
development sincethe late1960s.
We are writingto you today concerning Bill159, which proposes to amend chapters 19.11,19.12,19.14,
19.15,19.18,19.20,19.22,19.32 and 19.52 of the Maui County Code (MCC) and negativelyimpact short-term
rentalsinplanned developments such as Puamana. We are particularlyconcerned with the proposed
amendments to MCC section19.32.0401 as itdeals with planned developments, of which Puamana isone of
three on Maui.
We respectfullyurge Councilto rejectthe proposed amendments to MCC section 19.32.0401.
The reasoningbehind our positionissummarized below.
1. Aftersignificantdue diligenceand deliberation,MCC section 19.32.040 /was recommended by the
PlanningCommission and approved by a unanimous vote by Maui County Council in 2013. Itsexpress
purpose was to specificallycodify and permanently recognize long-standinghistoricrightsenjoyed by
the owners of Puamana {aplanned development) to engage in short-term rentals.Vacation rentalsat
Puamana have been occurringat Puamana for over 50 years sinceitwas builtinthe late1960s.
Additionalbackground information regardingthe historyisavailable
at: www.mauinews.eom/news/local-news/2013/01/panel-recommends-bi ll-allowing-puamana-tvrs/)
The proposed amendment to MCC section 19.32.040! w\\\be extraordinarilyprejudicialto the property
rightswhich owners of Puamana have enjoyed uninterruptedfor more than halfa century. The
"expresslypermissible"use wording currentlyinplacereflectsthe background to thisissueand
provides currentand prospectiveowners with an appropriate levelof comfort regarding theirhistoric
and ongoing rightsto engage in short-term rentals.Since 2013, many owners have reliedon this
legislationwhen purchasing unitsat Puamana. By changing the use from "expresslypermissible"to
1
"non-confirming" the abilityto rent Puamana unitsshort-term could be lostin a number of scenarios
includingdestructionby fireor flood with no rightto rebuild,owners ceasing rentalstemporarily,or
undertaking renovations over a certaindollaramount or alterationsto the buildingenvelope.
Puamana isa community with itsown roads,security,services,and recreationalamenities such as
swimming pools,sportscourtsetc.As a result,Puamana's guests tend to spend more time on the
property and their impact on the localinfrastructureisrelativelylow compared to visitorsstayingat
other propertiesaround the Island.
2.
Puamana owners have contributed substantiallyto Maui County's tax base over the past 54 years due
to theirproperty tax classificationas short-term rental.That tax revenue may be substantially
diminished under the current proposed legislation.
3.
The short-term rentalsat Puamana help support many localindependent businesses,some of which
work solelyin Puamana, such as cleaners,landscapers,appliance repair,maintenance, buildersand
their sub-trades to name a few. Ifshort-term rentals were prohibited in Puamana, thiswould have a
disastrous affect on the livelihood of those business owners and theiremployees.
4.
There isno opportunity for furtherdensificationat Puamana so there islimitedprospect of Puamana
contributingto any increase intourism on Maui going forward. Furthermore, MCC 19.32.0401 cannot
be used to create any additionalvisitoraccommodations anywhere elseon Maui inthe futurebecause
itisspecificto planned unitdevelopments builtand operating as vacationrentalspriorto April1,1981.
So MCC 19.32.040 Iessentiallyalready serves as a cap on TVRs in Puamana.
5,
In lightof the foregoing,we respectfullyrequest that the members of Maui County Councilrejectthisor any
other proposed legislationaimed at removing or diminishingthe rightsof Puamana owners to continue to use
theirpropertiesforshort-term rentalsas they have throughout the entirelifespanof thisdevelopment.
Thank you for your consideration.
Donna and Peter Gibson
43-1 Puamana

Moratorium Bill at Planning and Sustainable Land Use Thursday,
Then Council on Friday
The Transient Visitor Accommodations Cap Bill,or the Moratorium billwillbe
discussed on Thursday at the Planning and Sustainable Land Use Committee
Thursday at 10:30 am. This is Resolution 22-70. You can see the details
here: https://www.mauicountv.qov/DocumentCenter/View/134690/0809 22 Aqenda-
Item-B2 Bill5-for-Ord-Amend-Title-19 Transient-Accommodation-Cao s Memo-
Report
This measure was next scheduled for public hearing and review by the Maui Planning
Commission. However, itlooks likethe Council willbe exercising their rightto
preemptively not wait for the Planning Commission to finishdiscussion and report.
The Planning Commission has exceeded their 120 days for review and the Council
can now vote to proceed and hear the 1st reading on Friday.
1
We do not support this measure. We firmly believe in managed tourism and
regenerative tourism. However this measure does not have enough information
when itcomes to economic repercussions. We do not support changing property
uses described in the measure, and we feel the measure could accomplish itsgoal
without changing the use out from under property owners. We would liketo see
amendments to the language in the billto allow the existing properties continue
their use legally.
Note: This billdoes not impact bed and breakfast or short term rental permit
holders, and does not affect their abilityto renew their permits.
We have a current moratorium in place through January 7, 2024. We should be
exploring what our economic diversification plan is during this time, before making
this existing moratorium a permanent change.
The intent of this billis to cap transient vacation accommodation rental units at
existing levels.However there are several places in the department of planning
report recommended changes that indicate current TVR use in certain zones willbe
disallowed moving forward, and existing properties doing this use would be now
considered non-conforming.
At the very least the county should be contacting these properties that would be
affected.
(https ://mauicountv. leqistar.com/View.ashx?M = F&.ID=10639879& GUID=4DD9FFAE-
E750-49D8-B739-B844E9EDCAE2J
2
Details of the Proposed Bill
AccordingtoPlanningand SustainableLand Use Committee ReportNo.22-41,datedApril
22, 2022, the purposeof the proposedbillis to establishtransientaccommodationcaps as
recommended by the Budget,Finance,and Economic Development Committee’sTemporary
InvestigativeGroup (TIG)on Tourism Management and EconomicDevelopment.The proposed
billkeepsthetransientaccommodationcaps ineach zoningdistrictatthecurrentnumber,thus
allowingforno new transientaccommodationunitsas outrightpermittedusesinmost zoning
districts.
In additionto amending thezoning districts,the billalsoproposestostopcamping and
rentalrecreationalvehiclesparkedon the sideof roads,at beaches,and in countyparksby
prohibitingvehiclesfrom temporarilyparkingin allzoningdistrictsifused as short-term
accommodations unlesstheyareallowedby zoning and theproperpermitsarcobtained.

This resolution has raised a red flag with the county real property tax division.
Administrator Marcy Martin indicated in a letterto the Planning Department on
June 6 that there are concerns with the legislationthat pertains to the financial
repercussions of this measure.
Martin states "If a property with TVR or timeshare entitlements loses their
entitlements, assessed values and classificationcould be impacted. For
example, classificationwould change from hotel and resort or short term
rental to a lower tax rate classification. This bill could reduce real property tax
revenue. The impact cannot be measured without a market analysis of
impacted properties."
This year the county approved over $1.07 billiondollars for their FY2022
budget. For the firsttime in Maui's history we are going over 1 billiondollars.
This willbe more than a $200 Million increase, or 27% over lastfiscalyear.
The county funds most of those dollars in real property tax revenue. In all,the
county willraise $430 Million in property tax revenue this fiscalyear.
The short term classification will raise $160 Million in RPT tax, 12% more than
lastyear. This was an increase of $17 Millionin tax dollars,the highest
increase in allthe tax classifications.This year short term rentals represent
37% of the real property tax revenue, and 15% of the county of Maui's entire
operating budget.
Much of the increases in revenue in property taxes overall came from the
increase in values of properties. Total assessments rose $4 Billionoverallin
Maui County in fiscalyear 2022-2023. Increases in assessed values were 5%
overall in the short term classification. Short term rentals will contribute $12.1
Million in revenue to the Affordable Housing Fund, the largest contribution of
allthe classifications,and the largest contribution to date. Over the last5
years the short term rental classificationhas generated $31.5 milliondollars
for the affordable housing fund.
Gutting funding categories for the county does not make good fiduciarysense
given the current budget. Changing the property rights of owners without
notice to those property owners for comment is problematic and should not be
the way our county makes changes.
5

OFFICE OF HAWAIIAN AFFAIRS
Testimony of SylviaM. Hussey, Ed.D.
CEO I Ka Pouhana
Maui County Council
Bill154 (2022)
A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLES 18, 19 AND 20, MAUI COUNTY CODE, TO
ESTABLISH CULTURAL OVERLAY DISTRICTS
October 10, 2022 Council Chamber9:00 am
The Administration of the Officeof Hawaiian Affairs(OHA) offersthe following
COMMENTS on Bill154 (2022),which would establisha framework for culturaloverlay districts
with the intentto preserve and protect Native Hawaiian traditions,practices,culture,cultural
resources,and the integrityof the 'ainato which these facets(and more) of Native Hawaiian
identityhave become affixed.
OHA wishes to emphasize itssupport for the thrust of the measure to proactively
protect the broad scope of intereststhat interconnect and intersectwith constitutionally
protected Native Hawaiian rights.Such a measure has the potentialto prove itselfas an
equitable solutionin addressing long-standingsystemic issuesthat have undermined Native
Hawaiian existence in these islands.
Inthe hope of realizingthe far-reachingbenefitof thismeasure's purpose, OHA
expresses concerns that the absence of a culturaloverlaydistrictdesignationmay suggest that
that districthas no culturalsignificance,or that the Native Hawaiian culturalpracticestherein
are not significantenough to warrant protections.OHA stronglybelievesthat allthe lands,seas,
and atmospheric spaces of the Hawaiian Islands,whether remaining pristineor restingbeneath
modern urban expanse, are of ongoing culturalsignificance,especiallyto the Native Hawaiian
people.
OHA also expresses concerns with this measure's quantificationof significance,
moreover, OHA isdeeply concerned that thisquantificationisbased on the determination of
the county's principalarchaeologist,who isessentiallygranted the soleauthority- over the
Native Hawaiian community-in determining the levelof culturalimportance. Quantifyingthe
importance of a culturallysignificantpracticeor place,potentiallyover another,would be
destructivewhere the totalityof Native Hawaiian cultureshave come to definethe extentof
Native Hawaiian identity.
Finally,the 'olelono'eau (NativeHawaiian proverb},mai kaula'iwale ika iwio na
kupuna (never dry out,inthe sun,the bones of your ancestors),figurativelyand literally
expresses a traditionalruleinculturalsensitivityassociated with countless Native Hawaiian
traditionaland customary culturalpractices.The ruleholds that one shouldn't discuss,too
freely,certainmatters of significance.Inaccordance with thisrule,many Native Hawaiian
culturalpractitionersare reluctantto reveal detailedInformation about theirculturalpractices,
includingthe locationofwahi pana/wahi kapu (storiedand sacred sites).Any framework that
requiresNative Hawaiian culturalpractitionersto revealmore than they are comfortable,
would serve to erode the integrityof those practicesand theirrespectiveplaces.
OHA appreciatesthe opportunityto providescomments on thismeasure.
Count^CletJc

Date: October 12, 2022
Maui County Council
Resolution 22-206 Eminent Domain Pohakea Watershed Lands
To:
RE:
Aloha Chairperson Alice Lee and Maui County Council Members,
Mahalo for your support of Resolution 22-206 authorizing proceedings in eminent domain
for the acquisition of Ma'alaea Mauka/Pohakea Watershed lands which passed on first
reading on October 7^^.
Questions have been raised over whether this 257 acre parcel is"watershed" land. The DLNR
DOFAW application for Legacy Lands funding explains how the 257 acres is part of the larger,
5,268 acre "Pohakea Watershed lands mauka of Maalaea Bay" (Section D(l), page 5 of the
grant application).The LLC agreed that these lands should be protected, and granted DLNR
the additional $1 million needed for the purchase.
Our goal continues to be to encourage the buyers of this property to willinglysellthe land to
Trust for Public Land and transfer it to DLNR Division of Forestry and Wildlifeto own and
manage the property to create the "Forest Reserve" with surrounding state conservation
lands. This is ultimately the highest and best use for the property, and willassist with the
priorityof restoring Ma'alaea Bay to address sedimentation and wildfireissues. Other reasons
for preserving this land are numerous - preserving the open space and scenic resources and
addressing trafficissues at this crossroads between Central and West Maui.
Those opposed have made their best effort to convince this Council of their desire to create
"100 workforce housing units" on the property, although only 21 ag lots are allowed with
the current agriculturalland designation. Council members know the facts. Please
encourage the property owner to proceed with the sale, earn good faithwith the
community, and make this long held dream of preserving these lands a reality.
This initiativewill provide Maui County vast resources in restoring Maalaea Bay, preserving
the valuable open space and scenic resources, expand the historicLahaina PaliTrailand create
parks and trailsfor the benefit of Maui's people for years to come.
It is criticalthat the entire 257 acre parcel be acquired, and that itbe done promptly within
FY23 since the funding has been approved and isavailablein the current budget year.
The public benefits and reasons for acquiring this property have been well-documented.
Mahalo for your continued support.
Sincerely,
Lyndon Ibele

Narrative descriptionof location,ecosystems,landuse,and human activityon the
propertyand inthesurroundingarea.
15.
The Pohakea Watershed Lands arelocatedalong Honoapi'ilaniHighway, themain accessroad
from central Maui to Lahaina and West Maui. The land spans two ahupua’a — Ukumehame and
Wailuku — locatedatthebase of Mauna Kahalawai. The propertyislocatedacrossthehighway
and mauka of the Maui Ocean Center,Ma‘alaea Shops,and Ma*alaea Harbor. Partof the
Ma‘alaea ConservationCorridor,thepropertyconnectswith nearby landmarks such as Kealia
NationalWildlifeRefuge, theNationalMarine Whale Sanctuary,Maui Ocean Center,Pacific
Whale Foundation headquarters,and a petroglyphsiteon adjacentstateland.
Average annual rainfallatthe siteis 10-20 inches. Fresh northeasttradewinds prevail,
frequentlyreachingspeedsgreaterthan25 milesper hour. The soilson theparcelarepartof the
alluvialplainsof Ka Ma‘alaea. Priorto human colonizationand subsequentdisturbance,the
subjectlandswere withinthelowland tropicalgrasslandand shrubland zone. Those biomes are
among the most impacted by human activitiesand intactexamples arenow extremelyrareinthe
Main Hawaiian Islands.The propertyisno exception,and was used forsugar cultivationand
pastureinthelastcentury.
The Lahaina Pali Trail,which traverses between the districtsof Wailuku and Lahaina,passes
through theproperty.The Lahaina PaliTrailisknown from historicmaps atleastdatingas far
back as 1885 and isthoughttohave been a partofthe ancientalaloa.A 1992 survey of the trail
found itto be relativelyintactfrom itswesterntenninusatHonoapiTlani Highway near Papalaua
to thewestern boundary of thisproperty.Although thehistoricmaps show thetrailcontinuing
through thenorthernportionsof thispropertyand on toward Wailuku, the surveyswere not able
to locateevidenceof it,presumably because ithad been destroyedby thegradingof theland for
agriculture.In 1994, the Board of Land and Natural Resources set aside the Lahaina Pali Trailas
a Na Ala Hele Trailunder theDivisionof Forestryand Wildlife.For convenience,the trailwas
routedthrough an existingroad along theboundary of the propertyto itseasternterminus at
HonoapiTlani Highway. Today, the Lahaina PaliTrailisone of themost populartrailson Maui
frequentedby residentsand visitorsfor itsdramatic landscapesand sweeping vistas.
The propertyincludeseasements forwater linesacrossadjacentparcels3-6-004:008 and 3-6-
004:003 owned by ADD, LLC and Waikapu Properties,respectively.The owner of the Pohakea

16. Identifyand discussthe typesof assessments,surveys,permits,and documented analyses
conducted regardingtheproperly.
In 2005, a number of studiesof the land were completed to supporta proposed“Ma‘alaea
Mauka” development beforethe landwas soldto a new owner in2008. The formerowner also
competed a FinalEnvironmental Impact Statement(FEIS) (2010)tosupporttheproposed
“Ghana Kai” development;as wellas a FinalEnvironmentalAssessment (EA) (2015)tosupport
a subsequentiterationof the proposed development.The 2010 FEIS includedan agricultural
assessment.Flora and Fauna assessment;Archaeological inventorysurvey.HydrologicalStudy
and Preliminarywatertestingreports;preliminaryengineeringreport-drainage,roads,water
systemand a studyfora new onsitewastewaterplant.Therewere alsoPhaseI,PhaseIIand
Phase IIIEnvironmental SiteAssessment reports.Some of thereportsoriginatedfrom the
original2005 development proposal.Some were completedatthetimeofthe2009 DraftEIS and
updated forthe2014-2015 Draftand FinalEA.

(1) Watershed protection.
Describewatershed structure,function,and mechanics (forexample,elevation/rainfallgradients,
substrate,vegetativecover,waterbodytypesand conditions,rechargedynamics,
disturbances/impainnents,solutions).
The propertyislocatedinthePohakea watershedwhich includesabout5,268acresofland
mauka (upslope)ofMa‘alaeaBay. The Pohakea watershedhasseveralgulches/streamsthatall
dischargeintoMa‘alaeaBay and theharbor.The watershedbeginsatthesummitofHanaula
within the West Maui Mountains at 4,616 feet above sea leveland flows south and east.The
slopeisrelativelysteepattheupperportionsoftheWest Maui Mountainswiththegrade
levelingoffconsiderablyattheproperty.Pohakea Gulch isthemajorfeaturewithinthe
watershed.Itisa deeplyincisedgulchwithwaterflowingdue eastwhere itentersculvert
systemsbeforereachingHonoapi'ilaniHighway. The majorstreamsassociatedwiththePohakea
Watershed alongwithsmallerunnamed gulcheshave ephemeralflowregimes,typicallyflowing
onlyduringstonnevents.Rock Land isthedominantsoiltypewithinthePohakeaWatershed.
Thissoiltypeisconsideredwelldrainedwithveryhighrunoffpotential.The parentmaterialfor
Rock Land isbasaltwithsiltyclaimloam found between zerotofourinchesofthesurface,silty
claylocatedbetween fourtoeightinchesdeep,and bedrockfromeightto20 inchesofthe
surface.Depth tothewatertableistypicallygreaterthan80 inches.
5
DLNR/DOFAW with TPLApplicantName (Agency orNonprofit):
emailaddressforApplicantPointofContact:scott.fretz@hawaii.gov
The Pohakea StormwaterManagement Plan (2018)indicatedtheareahasfailedornon-
flinctioninginfrastructure,and improperor outdatedlandmanagement strategies.Unimproved
roads and powerlinecorridorsactas stormwaterconveyance mechanismsduringraineventsand
channel stormwaterand sediment intothegulches.Extensivehead cuttingwithinthestream
channelshave ledtothe lossof many tonsof sedimentmaterialduringstormevents,possibly
due theculvertsbeingundersized.The landscapeisdegradedwithareasdevoidofvegetationand
isdominated by invasivegrassesand weeds. Runoff from thePohakea WatershedLands have
highconcentrationsofammonia, organicnitrogen,phosphorus,and orthophosphates.The coastal
areasoffMa‘alaea do not meet theHawaii Statewater qualitystandardsand Ma‘alaea Bay is
consideredan impairedbody of water.Hillslopestabilization,head cutstabilization,restoration,
and vegetativebarrierswillhelp capturesedimentand promote the infiltrationof stormwater
sheetflow intotheground.
(2) Coastal areas, beaches, and ocean access.
Describe significantfeaturesand characteristicsthecoastal/marineenvironment,and thetype
and extent of access to shoreline,beaches, and ocean.
Stormwater from the Pohakea Watershed Lands directlyflows intoand negativelyimpacts
Ma‘alaea Bay. Land use and management thatprotectsvegetationand topsoilresourcesupslope
on the Pohakea Watershed Lands will reduce erosion and resultincleanerrunoffwater entering
The busy and popular Ma‘alaea Harbor area.Less sediment enteringMa'alaea Bay willimprove
water qualityforocean-based recreationand willalsobe healthierforcoralreefecosystems.
(3) Habitat protection.
Describetheplantand animal habitatsand populationslocatedwithinthepropertyand on
adjacentlands,including:
● Habitattype,location,elevation,extent,condition,and Federal/Statelegaldesignation
(such as criticalhabitat,wildliferefuge,etc.).
● Species,location,range,size,diversity,and Federal/Statelegal/biologicalstatus(suchas
threatened,endangered,invasive,noxious)of plantand animal populations.
Priorto human disturbance,theproposed landswere characterizedby lowland grasslandand
shrub ecosystems. The naturalresourcesof theproposed landsarenow highlydisturbedand
degradedfrom centuriesof agriculturaluse. Though disturbancehas been extensive,thelands
maintainrestorationpotentialthatwould benefittheHawaiian hoary bat,nene,and nativeplant
speciesthatareexpectedtobe components of habitatrestoration.Importantly,thesubjectparcel
and adjacentlandsarethreatenedby highlydamaging cyclesof fast-movingfiresthatremove
vegetation,followedby heavy rainsthatdestabilizesoilsand resultin massive erosionevents
thatfoulthenear shoreand coralreefhabitatsdownslope. Itiscriticalthatthose threatsare
addressed on both the subjectand adjacentlandsinorderforhabitatmanagement effortstobe
successful.Following purchase,thepartnerswillbegin implementationof applicableexisting
plansand development of a new forestreservemanagement forthe contiguousmanagement of
the subjectparceland the adjacentstatelands.
Effectiveplanningforconservationof naturalresourcesisessentialfor successfuleffortsto
conservenaturalresourcesand preventand suppresswildland fires.There are a number of

Firebreaks. Effectivefirebreaksarean importantlineofdefenseforthepreventionand
suppressionofwildlandfires.DOFAW maintainsapproximately18 milesoffirebreaksinwest
Maui, includingseveralmilesof breakson themauka landsofthePohakeaWatershed.In2020,
Maui Nui Marine ResourcesCouncilexpanded thatwork tothesubjectparcel,creatingan
additional3.5milesof firebreaksalongboth sidesofthelengthoftheparceladjacenttothe
highway makai and tothestatelandsmauka. DOFAW iscurrentlyplanningtoexpandthose
firebreicsbyaddingthreeconnectingcrossbreakstotheparcel,includinga numberofgreen
breaks,fora totalof 4.5 miles of breakson theparcel.
Water. Purchaseof thesubjectparcelby thecountyisexpectedtoincludepurchaseofthree
wells,a 750,000-gallontankand easementforthedeliveryofwateracrossadjacentlands.The
inclusionof thosewater resourceswith thepurchaseprovidessignificantbenefitsforthe

DLNR/DOFAW with TPLApplicantName (Agency orNonprofit):

management ofthesubjectlands,includingfiresuppression,habitatrestorationandmanagement
thatwillenabletheconstructionof green breaks,reforestation,and establishmentofvegetation
forthe controlof erosionthatdamages coralreefand nearshoremarine environments.
Habitatmanagement. The dryand windy conditionsoftheMa‘alaeaarea,coupledby thevery
flashyfuelspresenton thesubjectparceland adjacentlands,arehighlyconducivetotherapid
spreadofwildfires.The purchaseofthesubjectparcel,alongwiththewatereasementsthatare

Ignitionsources.Power linesand associatedstructuresaresuspectedtobe a sourceof ignition
on lands adjacentto the subjectparcel.DOFAW isworking with Hawaiian Electricand partners
to review potentialsourcepointsand plan and implement measures to reduce ignitionfrom those
sources.Preliminaryassessmentof sourcesincludesa seriesof powerlinesand polesrunning
mauka from thesubjectparcel.Following the assessment,DOFAW expecst Hawaiian Electric

Erosion control.Erosionof soilson the subjectparcelscontributesto thedepositof large
volumes of sedimentsintothe ocean atMa‘alaea Bay duringperiodsof heavy rain,threatening
coralreefecosystems and the economic, recreational,and subsistenceactivitiesthatdepend on
thoseresources.Frequentfiresexacerbatetheproblem by burning vegetation,renderingthe soils
bare and exposed to loss.Management activitiestorestorevegetationand reduce fireswillassist

improvement, and while thosefunds arenot currentlyavailableto supportthoseefforts,DOFAW
and community partnersare activelyseekingto securethose funds through state,federal,and
privategrantopportunities.

poisedtoactivelyparticipate.The Ma‘alaea VillageAssociationhas been a leaderin these

and realizethe community’s visionforthe landsatMa‘alaea and Pohakea Watershed.
