TESTIMONY IN SUPPORT OF BILL 159 to be heard on the C^uml^SUfQirAjdrfda
OUNTY CLERK
From:
Sent:
To:
Cc:
Subject: on
October 21, 2022
You don'toftenget emailfrom laura.legge@icloud.com.Learnwhy thisisimportant
\/lauiCounty Council:
Please accept thistestimony inSUPPORT of Bill159 “ A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE
COMPREHENSIVE ZONING ORDINANCE RELATING TO TRANSIENT ACCOMMODATION CAPS.”
We have owned our home on the Southside of Maui for 20 years and our familyhas been coming to Maui since
the 1920s. Yes, you read thatcorrectly.
Enough isenough. Maui County iscompletelyout of balance and everyone who callsMaui islandhome
experiences thisimbalance every singleday. Maui doesn’texistsolelyfortourism.
The Maui islandplan passed in2012 callsforthe number of visitorsto be no more than one-thirdof the residential
population.Clearlythisisnot being adhered to.
We do not need more shortterm rentals.We need long-termhousing solutions. Time and time again we are asked
by our friendsifwe know of any availablerentals,letalone affordablelong term rentals.Why aren’tthey
available? Because of greed. Too many homes on our Southside have been converted to shortterm rentals,
includingB&Bs.
And don’t tellme that those who work for the hotels willsufferifthisBillpasses. Just thisweek itwas reported that
Hawaii has the highest-earninghotelbusinesses inthe nation and thatMaui hotelscontinue to increase revenue per
availableroom sincethe pandemic in2019. Every singlehotelon the Southside iscurrentlyadvertisingformore
workers.
Don’t get me startedon the devastation of our Southside beaches and reefs I’vewitnessed over the past 30 years
caused by too many visitors,too many condos being builtmauka and too many homes on the beaches (thatliterally
sitempty because the homeowners are off-islandatone of theirother mansions inthe world).Meanwhile, the
wetlands and reefsforeverdestroyed. Our keikiwillblame our generation, as they should, ifwe don't get this
overuse reversed.
As we Southsiders know, the trafficon Piilaniand South Kihei Road has become intolerable. And don’t even think
about gettinga parkingspot at Makena Landing or Ulua after7:30 a.m. Nope. Alltaken by the visitors.
And where isallthe needed water fornew development going to come from? My understanding iswe don’thave
enough now. And what about the waste water created by additionaldevelopment? Are we going to put even more
partiallytreatedwaste water intoour ocean via injectionwells? Bacterialcounts at Kalama are already through the
roof.
This island is out of balance, and we allknow it.it’snot too lateto turn itaround. Please do the rightthing and pass
this Bill.
Mahalo nui loa
1
The Legge-Welter Family

FREC LIVEDDear Planning Commission,
im pCT19 PH2'-25I ask the Planning Department to recommend removing the proposed
changestosection19.32.040Iforplanneddevelopments^^^^''^ CLE^KBack in 2013 a billwas passed to allow short-term rentalsTbVPlanned
development like Puamana. Puamana was builtin the late 60's and has been
operating with vacation rentals since itsbeginning (around 53 years). It is a
230-unit development on 30-acres and there is no availabilityor possibility
of building new/more units. Puamana has itsown roads, security, and
amenities and does a pretty good job of containing tourist making their
impact much less on the Island as a whole. The few things that Puamana
doesn't have are restaurants and shopping, which isgreat for the
surrounding community as this supports small businesses throughout
Lahaina and the rest of Maui.
: I
The operation of short-term rentals within Puamana helps a number of small
businesses survive on Maui: cleaning companies, maintenance companies,
appliance repair companies, management companies, gardening services,
snorkel/beach bike rentals, photographers, etc. I feelthat you need to be
aware of who willactually be affected by this change.
According to a study done by Jen Russo of Maui Vacation Rental Association
about the Real Property Tax*, STR's contribute the most to the Real Property
Tax, in digging deeper, Puamana is in the top 10 complexes of revenue
generated for the County of Maui through real property tax. Out of the top
10, 7 are STR's and 3 are Hotels. I think this would a be huge unintended
consequence for changing the PUD zoning to non-conforming in this bill.
Again, I ask the planning department to recommend removing the proposed
changes to section 19.32.40 for planned developments within Resolution
22.70.
Thank you for your time,
Andy Marchello

● Reference Committee Report No. 22-98 regardingResolution22-206.

inadequate numbers of teachersdue to the lackof housing.
Many of our non profitsand localbusinesses are forced into debt tryingto provide serviceswith no means or pathway
to ever obtainhousingof theirown or operationalland for program development.

visionforsomething new.

leaders.

We have to do better.Ihope you willlookatyour decisionsand decide againstthisidea alltogether.

From:

Aloha,
1am a 20 year residenton Maui, livingin the Kiheiareathe entiretime.As many are aware,theislandissuffering
with the huge influxofvisitors.We allknow the Maui Islandplanpassed in2012 callsforthe number ofvisitorsto
be no more than one thirdof the residentialpopulation,or 33%. The visitorinfluxiswreaking havoc on our
sensitiveinfrastructure,upsettingresidentswho can'tfindparkingattheirlocalbeaches,but do gettofindshelves
empty atthe supermarkets.We hear horror storiesofvisitorsbuying beach equipment atCostco,onlytoreturnthe
items on theirway to the airport,and boasting about iton socialmedia. Costco can'treselltheseitemsso theyend
up inour ever increasinglandfill.This isan unsustainablesituation.
Currently,in mid-October, when we used to have a lullinvisitorarrivals,we are experiencingon the south sidean
insane amount of traffic.Yes, there isconstruction going on, but justlastyear [priorto constructionstart),getting
stuck atthe Lipoa Streetstoplightwould findyou backed up tosouthofHope Chapel.Now we are backed up tothe
policestation,and atpau hana time,as workers commute home from thehotels,trafficisbacked up even further.
[See Pi'ilaniHighway photos.)
So one thinks,maybe betterto go South KiheiRoad. Tried thattoday,October 19th,at 10:30am, and thattoo, was
backed up. [See SKR photo.)
Unfortunately,the planning commission justapproved another 1,000 homes on the south side.Then thereisthe
constructionprojectoccurring in Makena. Heaven knows the trafficimpactthesethousands ofcarswillhave.
Let'sdiscusswater. Where isitallcoming from? Willyou startdemanding thathotelsconserve water as we
residents have been asked to do? Do the short term vacation rental owners request visitorsto conserve water? I
doubt it.
This isutterlyunsustainable,and Ifearwe willrun out ofwater completely,and willlosethebettervisitorwho
actuallyspends money here [ratherthan the folkson socialmedia who adviseotherstobringtheirown
condiments and pack theirown frozen meats in theircarryons).
Please,help us save thisonce idyllicislandby approving Bill159,theVisitorAccommodation Moratorium.It’sa
step inthe rightdirection,with another step being the completionofthe North-SouthCollectorRoad.
Mahalo for considering my testimony.
Eileen McKee

RE: BILL 159- A BILL FOR AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COMPREHENSIVE ZONING
ORDINANCE RELATING TO TRANSIENT ACCOMMODATION CAPS
My name isPane Meatoga IIIand Iam the Community Liaisonforthe Hawaii Operating Engineers
IndustryStabilizationFund (HOEISF). We are a labormanagement fund representing3000 unionized
members inheavy engineeringsitework and 500 general contractorsspecializinginheavy siteand
vertical construction. Our organization opposes Bill159 as itis currently written and recommend
amendments.
We understand that there are issues with over tourism on the islandof Maui. Unfortunately,Bill159 as
itiscurrentlywritten willhave severe negative impacts to Maui's economy, itsconstructionindustry,
and forthe existinguses currentlyallowed by law and permitted forcurrenthomeowners. We are also
worried thatthe expedited pace of thisproposed legislationdoes not allowforproper publicinput.
There are a lotof issuesand confusion by stakeholdersaffected by thisbill.
HOEISF would like to recommend amendments that will remove "accommodations caps" inthe
appropriatelyzoned areas of Hotel Districtsand Business-ResortCommercial Districtswith no
conditionaluse permit requirements.The billshould alsoallowforexpansionoftimeshare unitswithin
Hotel Districts.
We look forward to seeing Bill159 amended to mitigatenegativeimpactsto homeowners, stakeholders,
and Maui's economy.
Mahalo,
Community Liaison
Hawaii Operating EngineersIndustryStabilizationFund
UNITED OUR STRENGTHS AND WORKING TOGETHER FOR A BETTER TOMORROW

bill 159
From:
Sent:
To:
Subject:
You don'toftenget emailfrom david.w.medina@gmail.com.Learnwhy thisisimportant
am the owner of 58-2 Pualoke Place in Puamana.
Ihereby objectto the proposed language of Bill159 which seeks to deletethe currentlanguage in Maui County
Code 19.32.040 I(“Code”)and accordinglychange the status of short-term rentaluse at Puamana from a
permissibleuse intoan existingnon-conforming use.
This sectionofthe Code appliesonlyto unitsinPuamana. Kaanapali Plantationand Alaeloa thatwere builtand
used forTransient Vacation rentalpriorto April20, 1989. Itdoes not allow any new visitoraccommodations to be
builtor converted from residentialto TVR use. This part of the Code was established in 2013 to clarifythe long
standing legalTVR uses inthese specificprojectsand helps the planning department when approving building
permits and SMA exemptions forremodels and renovations of these 40-60-year-old units.The proposed deletion
turnsthe legalTVR use intoan “existingnon-conforming”use and makes any renovations or remodels difficultto get
permit approvals.This inmy view isunwarranted and should be rejected by the Council.
In additionto the above, itwould appear thatthe Planning Commission was not consulted fortheirrecommendation
with respect to the proposed deletionto the Code. Itwould also appear thatthe short-termvacation rentalindustry,
which is vitalto the economic lifeand health of the County, has not been afforded any opportunityto share its
concern with the Council or the Commission and address the significantpitfallsand problems inherent in this
proposed change..
Accordingly,Irequest thatthisportionof Bill159 which seeks to delete the current language in Maui County Code
19.32.040 Ibe rejectedoutrightor alternativelythisportionof the Billreturned back to committee to allowthe
Planning Commission to complete itsreview (withinputfrom the short-termvacationrentalindustry)beforeany
furtherconsiderationisgiven to thisproposed change to the Code.
Thank You
C V .

Please submit the followingtestimony relatedto the proposed Bill159.
Ioppose the proposed language of Bill159 which seeks to delete the currentlanguage in Maui County Code
19.32.040 I(“Code”)which was establishedto clarifythe statusof long standing vacation rentalsin Puamana and
other West Maui communities. This clarificationhelps the planning department when approving buildingpermits and
SMA exemptions forremodels and renovations of these 40-60-year-old units.The proposed language would
change the longstanding statusinthese communities which were builtand used forTransient Vacation Rentals prior
to April20, 1989 from a permissibleuse intoan existingnon-conforming use. Please rejectthischange and consider
possible alternativesolutionsthatmeet community needs while also protectinglong-standingapproved use inthese
developments and returnBill159 back to the Planning Commission to allow foradditionalreview and solutions.
Thank you forthe opportunityto testifyvia email.
Sincerely,
Irene Miller,Trustee

From:

BOUNTY CLERKSubject:
I You don’toften get email from lindafinearts@gmail.com.Learnwhy thisisimportant
To the Maui Council,
Please do not pass Resolution22-70.
I do not support this measure. I firmly believe in managed tourism and regenerative
tourism. However this measure does not have enough information when itcomes to
economic repercussions. I do not support changing property uses described in the
measure, and I feel the measure could accomplish itsgoal without changing the use out
from under property owners. I would liketo see amendments to the language in the bill
to allow the existing properties continue their use legally.
The intent of this billisto cap transient vacation accommodation rental units at existing
levels. However there are several places in the department of planning report
recommended changes that indicate current TVR use in certain zones willbe disallowed
moving forward, and existing properties doing this use would be now considered non-
conforming.
Implementation of this billwillresult in loss of jobs and taxes collected.
Thank you,
Linda Mitchell

months ago and 1have been unable to get her intoher therapistseven withnumerous
phone callsto kaiser.She feelsunsafe on Maui so has moved to Oahu to be withfamily

feltsafeto stay here with her familyifkaiserhad providedthe care we deserve.Shortly

5.22
1am in oppositionto Bill159 [2022] amending the comprehensive zoning ordinance
relatingto transientaccommodations.
Where the followingisstatedin the Bill...
" Ifany buildingor structureapproved or lawfullyexistingisreconstructed,renovated,
or expanded, then the transientvacation rentaluse islimitedto the originalbuilding
envelope."

My testimony on Bill159
To:
Subject:
I You don'toftengetemailfrom deboraheyem@gmail.com. Learnwhy thisisimportant
The Maui community supports a cap. and we want to prioritizethe qualityof lifeforour
residents first.
I have livedon Maui forover 45 years, and the topicof creatinga more diversified
economy has been discussed formany decades, with no actiontaken towards a viable
solution.Over tourism issimply not sustainableforthe aina,forthe people, or forthe
environment. Maui residentsagree thatwe already have too many visitors,yet the hotel
development industrywants to keep buildingmore, using massive amounts ofwater
that hotels use in abundance.
Every new home means more water usage. Ifthere isa water shortage itisthe local
people who are expected to rationwater so the hotelshave more availability.
Overtourism isa serious problem affectingour qualityof life,and people are lookingfor
solutions.We can't control what the airlinesdo, so the best way to remedy over tourism at
the County levelisto limitwhere people can stay on Maui.
When 1firstmoved here tourism was primarilyin Lahaina. Soon, tourism spread to Kihei
Paia, Makawao and leftno area not affected and transformed into less than ideal living
situationsbecause of so many cars,so many tourists,and not enough space fora
more "traditionalway of life"that residentshave long enjoyed.
Maui isnow one largetouristdestination,and the localswho livehere now have to drive
the roads during certainhours to avoid so much congestion. During covidwe allsaw the
thousands of rentalcars parked near Costco thatwere allon roads thatsimply do not
have the infrastructurein place to accommodate thousands more vehicles.
Ifwe do not cap tourism we willcontinue down thisnever ending slipperyslope towards all
of Maui becoming justanother Waikikior another Honolulu squished on Maui.
Your vote isvotingeither formore water usage by more development, more cars on the
roads, more congestion, or against uncontrolleddevelopment.
Support the Hawaiian Way of Lifeby votingFOR A CAP ON TOURISM
I
We are watching your vote.
SincerelyI
Deborah Maika'ikalaniPozin

existingoperatingproperties.Amend theexistinglanguageto say theexistingpropertiesdoing thisuse can
continuewith legaluse.Restrictfutureuses,but do not change the existingpropertyuse.This isstillin linewith
the intentof the proposal.
The county’soperatingbudget has increasedtoover 1 Billiondollars.Most ofthecounty’srevenuecomes from
the shortterm rentalclassification.The county of Maui has long had a strategyof taxingthe ShortTerm Rental
Classificationinordertokeep taxeslow fortheresidents.A bigpartof thisstrategyisthepartofthe
assessmentsof theseproperties.

Ifyou look atthistableof shortterm classifiedand hotelclassifiedtaxedproperties,you can seethatthe
assessment of many shortterm rentalsresultina higherrateand taxrevenue than many of our hotelproperties.
One of the toolsused by the assessment divisionisthe factthattheshortterm rentalsaresoldmore frequently
on the real estate market and then these sales are factoredintothetaxablevalue of theproperties.Thus the
assessed values in the short term rental class are some of thetop realpropertytaxvaluedpropertieson the
island,generatingmost ofthetaxrevenueforthecounty.
The assessedvaluesof propertiesareaffectedby theuse designatedtotheseproperties.Decisionsthatthis
body makes that affectthe property values,can alsonegativelyaffectthe bottom linefor realproperty
tax.Any declinein revenue in the hoteland shortterm rentalclasscouldresultinan increaseintaxesfor
residents.
Ifyou look atPuamana forexample, thatisthe 8thlargestrevenuegeneratingproperty(forpropertiesclassified
as shorttemi rentalor hotel).The measure seeks to change theuse forthispropertywhich willaffectthe
$296,000,000 million in assessment value thatresultsinthecollectiverealpropertytaxofabout $1.6million.
This propertyhas had thislegaluse since1970. In a yearwhere we have reliedupon theshorttermrentalclass
to bear increases to fund our over a billion dollar operatingbudget,itisbafflingforthecounciltomake these
kinds of changes totheuse forthisproperty,withouttheproperdiscussionfrom theplanningcommission,input
from thepropertyowners and thesmall businessesthattheysupport,aswellasa formalmarketanalysisofthe
impact.
The Lahaina HistoricDistrictraisesa significantamount ofrevenueforpropertytax.The propertiesinthis
districtaccommodating our visitorsare an importantpartofourhospitality.Stayinginthehistoricdistrictcan
reallydemonstratethe significanceand historyof Lahaina.The gueststhatseekoutthesestaysarethekindsof
guestsMaui wants.
This resolutionhas raised a red flagwith the county realpropertytax division.AdministratorMarcy
Martin indicatedina letterto the Planning Department on June 6 thatthereareconcernswiththelegislationthat
pertainstothe financialrepercussionsof thismeasure.
Martin states‘Tfa propertywith TVR or timeshareentitlementslosestheirentitlements,assessedvaluesand
classificationcouldbe impacted.For example,classificationwould changefrom hoteland resortorshortterm
rental to a lower tax rate classification. This bill could reduce realproperty tax revenue. The impact cannot
be measured without a market analysisof impacted properties.”
Page 3140 Hoohana St. Ste. 210, Kahului, HI 96732-2467
M A UI
VACATION RENTALA S S O CIATIO N
This yearthecountyapproved over $1.07billiondollarsfortheirFY2022 budget.For thefirsttimeinMaui’s
historywe are going over 1 billiondollars.This willbe more thana $200 Millionincrease,or 27% over last
fiscalyear.The county fundsmost ofthosedollarsinrealpropertytaxrevenue.In all,thecountywillraise$430
Millioninpropertytaxrevenue thisfiscalyear.
The short term classification will raise $160 Million in RPT tax,12% more than lastyear.This was an
increaseof $17 Millionintax dollars,the highestincreaseinallthetax classifications.This year shortterm
rentalsrepresent37% of therealpropertytaxrevenue,and 15% ofthecountyof Maui’s entireoperatingbudget.
What thisdemonstrates isthat the county depends on the tax revenues of propertieslikethe ones
operating in the districtsthat would be affectedby this measure.
Much of the increasesinrevenue inpropertytaxesoverallcame from theincreaseinvaluesof properties.Total
assessmentsrose$4 BillionoverallinMaui County in fiscalyear 2022-2023. Increasesinassessedvalueswere
5% overall in the short term classification. Short term rentalswill contribute $12.1 Million in revenue to the
AffordableHousing Fund, the largestcontributionof alltheclassifications,and thelargestcontributionto date.
Over the last5 years the short term rentalclassificationhas generated $31.5 million dollarsfor the
affordable housing fund.
Guttingfunding categoriesforthe county does notmake good fiduciarysensegiventhecurrentbudget.
Changing thepropertyrightsof owners withoutnoticetothosepropertyowners forcomment isproblematicand
should not be theway our County makes changes.
I am surethereisa way forthiscouncilto finda method forward with thismeasure thatdoes not remove the
propertyrightsinthesedistrictsfortheexistingproperties.Amend theexistinglanguagetosay theexisting
propertiesdoing thisuse can continuewith legaluse.Restrictfutureuses,butdo not change theexisting
propertyuse.This isstillin linewith the intentof theproposal.
Thank you forconsideringmy testimony.

Testimony - Bill68
To:
OPf ICE OF THE
COUNTY CLErv^Subject:
I You don'toften get email from kevin.b.spellman@co.maui.hi.us.Learn why thisisimportant
Maui County Council
200 S.High St.
CouncilChamber, KalanaO Maui Building8th Floor
Wailuku, HI 96793
October 20, 2022
Subject:Testimony Regarding Bill68
To Maui County CouncilMembers,
Irespectfullypropose thatBill68 forthe additionof Chapter 3.97to the Maui County Code to establisha managed retreat
revolvingfund to address development needs as a resultof shorelineerosiondue to climatechange and risingsea levels,
returnto the Budget, Finance,and Economic Development Committee fora fundamental re-drafting.Isuggest Bill68
containtwo core sectionsbased on the ownershipof realpropertyand relatedassets:personaland commercial.The
currentmechanisms withinBill68 regardingestablishinga managed retreatrevolvingfund are only suitableforpersonal
property and associatedassets.Shorelineerosion and subsequent requirements forshiftingexistingand new development
away from the shoreline,perhaps even beyond the specialmanagement area (SMA), isnot a sudden problem. Maui
County commercial entitieshave had yearsto save fora stormy day,and as such,they bare the entiretyof responsibility
forthe costsrelatedto managed retreat.The properallocationof liabilityforthe costsof managed retreatforcommercial
entitiesnotwithstanding.Bill68 isan opportunityfor Maui County to assistcommercial entitiesviaan investment
approach. Suppose a commercial entity,such as those in Kahana, must fortifyor relocateassetsaway from the shorelineor
beyond the SMA. Ratherthan offeringdirectpayments,grants,or even loansto the commercial entity,Maui County
should,viaa specialpurpose development agency,become a shareholderof the enterprise,with a positionon the
executiveboard,which includesveto rightsover administrationand operationactivities.Inreturnforthe investment
provided by the county to the commercial entityconnected with the requirementsof managed retreat,Maui County
should receivea percentageof quarterlyrevenueand a furtherportionof any profitsattained.Maui County should retain
the share of ownership and rightsuntil200% of the investment returnsto the specialpurpose development agency fund.
Followingthe completion of involvementwith the commercial entity,Maui County should publiclyauctionoffthe
associatedshares.Bill68 isan opportunityforMaui County to manage shorelineretreatforowners of personaland
commercial propertywhilesimultaneouslyincreasingrevenueforthe county ina manner unrelatedto taxation.
Thank you foryour time.
Kevin Spellman
108 Kealaloa Avenue
Makawao, HI 96768

My reasons for this request to include 19.32.040 Iare many:
This sectionof the County code appliesonly to unitsin Puamana, KaanapaliPlantationand Alaeloathatwere builtand
used forTransientVacation rentalpriorto April20,1989. Itdoes not allow ANY new visitoraccommodations to be built
or converted from residential to TVR use.

and helps the planning department when approving buildingpermits and SMA exemptions forremodels and
renovations of these 40-60 year old units.
The proposed deletionof thispartof the existingcode turnsthe legalTVR use intoan "existingnon conforming" use
and makes any renovations or remodels difficultto get permit approvals.
I feel that more voices need to be heard and do not feel this billhas been a collaborative effort.

work.

Board of Directors:
President
Kyle Caires Chair Lee and Members of the Council
Maui County Farm Bureau on behalf of our farm and ranch familiesand organizations
strongly supports with suggested amendments, Bill160 amending Chapter 22.04A,
Maui County Code, relatingto the expansion area of the Kula AgriculturalPark.

JoshuaShylohStaftord-Joncs
Secretary
JaysonWatts Phase 1 of the expansion provides an opportunity forexpansion of agricultural
production on Maui. It'slocationsuitsa variety of crops that long been associated
with Maui and its'proximity to the Universityof Hawaii FieldExperiment Station
provides technicalresourcesto the new farm tenants.
Treasurer
Tim Stevens
Directors:
We ask for reconsideration of two matters.
Committee make up: Reconsiderationof a GoFarm position.GoFarmispart
of the Universityof Hawaii CTAHR that already has a positionon the
committee. CTAHR has an extensive network of education outreach
programs.
While the applicationform requires a Soiland Water Conservation practice
plan as part of the farm plan,an areawide Conservation Planshould be
undertaken by the County priorto plotallocation.Some practices may cross
plot boundaries and such plans should be put intoplacewith applicantsaware
of the requirements.
Section 22.14A.085 This proposal prioritizesfood production over other crops.
Food Securityinvolvesplantingof nonfood crops.
Importation of non food nursery plantsand other ornamentals Isa major
source of invasivespecies that not only impact the environment but food
production. Localproduction of highlydesirablefoliagee.g.Myrtaceae
spp demanded by floristsfor bridesisan important step to protecting us
from Ohia Rust species.
Crop rotationisa criticalpartto maintain pestsand improving soilhealth.
This can involveplantingof non food speciesthat are oftentilledintothe
ground or could be sold.

Mahalo, in advance, for reading our testimony. This isalloriginalcontent from our
Ghana. Ihope thistestimony reaches you in time. Iapologize ifitisLate.
We ask that you, the Planning Committee, recommend removing the changes proposed
to section 19.32.040 for Maui PUDs to the Maui County Council.
The idea of our Puamana condo changing itsuse statuswould be detrimental to our
growing family here in west Maui. Our immediate family consistsof 5 adultsand 5
children who are positivelyactive and charitablein our Lahaina community and within
Maui county. We recently combined our family'sfunds to purchase a home in Puamana
lastyear 2021 with the knowledge that Puamana has been operating as Legalvacation
rentalsfor about 53 years since the firstphase was builtin the '60s.Itwas thishistory
and the idea of how our guests would shop, eat and participatein LocalLahaina small
businessesnearby that gave us the confidence and peace of mind needed to make such
an investment for our future. We would almost immediately be underwater on our
mortgage ifour unit use statuschanged from short-term vacation to anything else
thereby puttingour family’sfinancialfuture at risk. /
1
Itseems irresponsibleand a bitfrighteningto recommend such changes to section
19.32,040 so quicklyand without the necessary data and studiesconducted to overturn
this much historyand previous decisions by the council.
For these reasons, Iask that the planning department recommend removing the
proposed changes to section 19.32.040 for planned developments within resolution
22.70 CD1 FD1.
Aloha and Mahalo,
